    [Original] IF Copack LLC dba Initiative Foods Recalls â€œTippy Toesâ€ Brand Apple Pear Banana Because of Possible Health Risk
    More Recalls, Market Withdrawals, & Safety Alerts Sanger, CA â€“ February 13, 2026 â€“ IF Copack LLC d.b.a. Initiative Foods (â€œInitiative Foodsâ€) is recalling one lot of the â€œTippy Toesâ€ brand Apple Pear Banana Fruit puree (â€œProductâ€) due to elevated levels of patulin. Patulin is a naturally occurring substance (called a mycotoxin) which is produced by molds that may grow in various fruits, including apples. Long-term exposure resulting from ingestion of patulin can lead to various adverse health consequences, including a potential for immune suppression, nerve damage, headache, fever, and nausea. No illnesses or injuries have been reported to date. The Product was distributed nationwide in retail grocery stores in all U.S. states other than Alaska. The Product may have been distributed in the U.S. territories of Guam and Puerto Rico. 2-pack plastic tubs, with product information sleeve The â€œBest Byâ€ (expiration) date is found on the bottom of each plastic tub. The recalled Product will have a date stamped as â€œBB 07/17/2026.â€ The package is also marked with the package code â€œINIA0120â€ as shown below: The recalled Product was sampled under the Total Diet Study by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (â€œFDAâ€), which found elevated patulin levels higher than is common for these products. Initiative Foods worked with FDA to identify the single lot to recall due to possible health concerns identified in this notice. This recall is being conducted based on FDAâ€™s recommendation. Consumers with the Product matching the â€œBest Byâ€ (expiration) date of July 17, 2026 should: Retailers should check inventory and shelves, and immediately remove the affected lot from sale or distribution and catalogue the recalled product. â€œAt Initiative Foods, the safety of our consumers and their families is our highest priority. We are cooperating with the FDA to ensure strict review and enhanced safety measures across all our products. We thank our retail partners and customers for their understanding and prompt action on this matter,â€ said Don Ephgrave, Initiative Foodsâ€™ CEO and President. For further recall information and updates, consumers and retailers can call a dedicated toll-free number: 1-855-215-5730, Monday through Friday, 8 a.m. to 5 p.m. Eastern Standard Time. This recall is being conducted with the full knowledge of the U.S. Food and Drug Administration.

    [Original] Ambrosia Brands, LLC Recalls Rosabella Moringa Capsules Because of Possible Health Risk
    More Recalls, Market Withdrawals, & Safety Alerts Ambrosia Brands, LLC of New York, New York is recalling certain lots of its Rosabella Moringa Capsules product due to possible contamination with Salmonella, an organism which can cause serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, frail or elderly people, and others with weakened immune systems. Healthy persons infected with Salmonella often experience fever, diarrhea (which may be bloody), nausea, vomiting and abdominal pain. In rare circumstances, infection with Salmonella can result in the organism getting into the bloodstream and producing more severe illnesses such as arterial infections (i.e., infected aneurysms), endocarditis and arthritis. The recalled product was sold to consumers located nationwide in the United States, through our direct-to-consumer website (tryrosabella.com) and Tik Tok Shop (https://www.tiktok.com/shop/pdp/moringa-capsules-800mg-by-rosabella-for-immune-gut-health-support/1729464033034539782), since February 2025. We are also aware that there may be unauthorized 3rd party distribution to consumers through ebay.com, Shein, or other sites. None of the impacted lots were sold by us on Amazon.com, however, while we do not have any authorized resellers on Amazon.com, we urge you to check your lot numbers for any Rosabella Moringa capsules purchased on the site. The recall includes the following product and lots: The recalled products are packaged in white plastic bottles. The lot code is printed on the bottom of the bottles. The lot code is the middle seven digits of the code printed above the expiration date. Additionally, the affected product has expiration dates from 03/2027 to 11/2027. Please see the example packaging and lot code below. No other Ambrosia Brands products are impacted by this recall. To date, there have been 7 illnesses resulting in 3 hospitalizations across the United States due to Salmonella contamination, 3 of which may be linked to a single product. At this time, the FDA and CDC have reported that the outbreak may be linked to Rosabella Moringa Capsules. We continue to diligently investigate, in collaboration with FDA, this possible link of the Salmonella outbreak to Rosebella Moringa Capsules. We have discontinued use and purchase of all raw moringa leaf powder from the raw material supplier of the above referenced lots. Customers who have purchased the lots above are asked to dispose of it immediately, do not eat, sell, or serve the product. Ambrosia Brands is conducting this recall voluntarily and takes this matter very seriously. We apologize for the inconvenience and concern this recall may cause our customers. Our company is committed to ensuring the quality of our products and the well-being of our consumers. Consumers with questions may contact the company M-F from 9am-4pm CT at 914-768-1357.

    Costa Mesa, California â€” February 13, 2026 â€” Green Lumber Holding, LLC (â€œGreen Lumberâ€) is issuing an updated consumer alert regarding counterfeit products falsely marketed as genuine Green Lumber products that may pose potential health risks.

    [Original] Vertexâ€™s CRISPR therapy rebounds in latest earnings
    Sales of Casgevy, the CRISPR Therapeuticsâ€“developed gene-editing therapy for sickle cell disease and beta thalassemia, more than tripled in the fourth quarter of 2025, contributing to a 9% year-over-year revenue increase for Vertex Pharmaceuticals, which reported $12 billion in total revenueâ€”$3.2 billion in the fourth quarter. Casgevy generated $54 million in Q4 and $116 million for the full year, surpassing Wall Street expectations after sales of $17 million were reported in the third quarter. The number of patients initiating the Casgevy treatment process nearly tripled from 109 in 2024 to 301 in 2025. The therapy, which uses CRISPR to edit blood stem cells to produce fetal hemoglobin, can effectively cure the diseases, though the conditioning chemotherapy required before infusion can cause severe side effects, including infertility, deterring some patients. Of the 64 patients whose cells were reinfused in 2025, 30 received infusions in the final quarter. TD Cowen analyst Tyler Van Buren noted that sales may fluctuate quarterly due to the lengthy 12-month process and patient scheduling preferences, such as avoiding treatment during holidays. He projected Casgevy could reach $227 million in sales in 2026 based on the current patient pipeline. Vertex expects sales to â€œsmooth outâ€ by 2027 and expressed optimism about the robust patient flow, according to Chief Operating Officer Duncan McKechnie. The company also received a priority review voucher from the FDA for Casgevy in children aged 5 to 11 and plans to seek approval in the first half of 2026. This could significantly boost future revenue. Casgevyâ€™s performance was one of two â€œpositive surprisesâ€ in the earnings report, alongside strong sales of the new cystic fibrosis drug Alyftrek. Cystic fibrosis drugs, primarily Trikafta and Kaftrio, accounted for over $10 billion of the $12 billion in 2025 revenue. Vertex forecasts $13 billion to $13.1 billion in 2026 revenue, with $500 million or more from non-CF products, including the non-opioid pain drug Journavx and the experimental kidney drugs povetacicept and inaxaplin. Povetacicept, in a late-stage trial for IgA nephropathy, could generate at least $1.2 billion annually if approved, according to RBC Capital Markets.

    [Original] David J. Farber, â€˜Grandfather of the Internet,â€™ Dies at 91
    David J. Farber, widely regarded as the â€œgrandfather of the internetâ€ for mentoring pioneering figures in computer networking, died on February 7 in Tokyo at age 91. His son Emanuel confirmed the cause was heart failure. Farber had been teaching at Keio University since 2018. Beginning his career at Bell Laboratories in the mid-1950s, he helped transition computing from isolated machines to interconnected systems. He became a key architect of the internet through his mentorship of students who shaped foundational protocols. Among them were Jonathan Postel, whose 1974 dissertation defined early internet communication rules, and Paul Mockapetris, who co-designed the Domain Name System (DNS). Their work, developed during weekly meetings at a Southern California pancake house, formed the basis of academic networks that evolved into the internet. Farberâ€™s 1977 paper with Paul Baran, â€œThe Convergence of Computing and Telecommunications Systems,â€ argued that computers could handle communication tasksâ€”foreshadowing email and messagingâ€”and helped secure National Science Foundation funding for Arpanet expansion. He played a central role in projects like CSNet, NSFNET, and NREN, aiming to connect U.S. university computer science departments via standardized protocols. In 1991, Congress opened the network to nonacademic use, though Farber noted in 2007 that commercial applications were not envisioned initially. Born in Jersey City, N.J., on April 17, 1934, Farber earned a general engineering degree and a masterâ€™s in mathematics from Stevens Institute of Technology. He worked at Bell Labs, then RAND Corporation, where he developed multiple programming languages. He taught at UC Irvine, the University of Delaware, the University of Pennsylvania, and Carnegie Mellon before joining Keio. He also served as chief technologist at the Federal Communications Commission (2000â€“2001) and advised organizations like the Electronic Frontier Foundation and the Internet Society. Farber championed human-centered design, creating the influential â€œI.P.â€ mailing listâ€”â€œinteresting peopleâ€â€”which connected around 25,000 users and became a key source for internet policy updates. Known for his warmth and collaborative spirit, he emphasized that technical progress required people skills, proposal writing, and relationship-building. His son Emanuel said Farberâ€™s legacy lies in recognizing that â€œitâ€™s not just tinkering in the labâ€ but fostering collaboration that built the internet. Farber is survived by his son Emanuel, two grandchildren, and his late wife Gloria Gioumousis, who died in 2010. Another son, Joseph, died in 2006.

    [Original] Their Secret to a Happy Marriage? A Translation App
    David Duda, 62, and Hong Liang, 57, a married couple from New Haven, Conn., rely on eight external battery packs to keep their smartphones charged, as their relationship depends on real-time translation via Microsoftâ€™s Translator app. Duda speaks English; Liang speaks Mandarin. They met in Xiâ€™an, China, in 2019, when Dudaâ€™s brother arranged a tour, and Liang drove him around. After a brief encounter, they began communicating via WeChat, using text and online translation tools. When the pandemic isolated them, they deepened their bond through daily messages, sharing personal histories and emotions. In September 2022, Liang flew to the U.S. after China eased travel restrictions, arriving to find Duda holding a sign in Chinese that read â€œLove of my life.â€ She recalled being deeply moved, calling it â€œvery romantic.â€ Their communication remains reliant on the Microsoft Translator app, which converts spoken words into text in real time. They use it to navigate daily life, though it requires intense focusâ€”neither can multitask or walk away during conversations. Duda said the app forces them to be â€œmore in the moment,â€ enhancing intimacy. However, the technology is imperfect. During an interview using Apple AirPods and the app, misunderstandings occurred. For instance, when Liang described falling ill with Covid-19 shortly after arriving, the app translated â€œnovel coronaâ€ as â€œnew crown,â€ leading to confusion. Professor Wallace Chen of Middlebury College reviewed the exchange, noting the app failed on longer, nuanced statements and missed words when Liang spoke at length. Speech-to-text transcription often lagged or dropped words, especially in noisy environments. Despite these flaws, the couple finds the system manageable. Duda granted Microsoft permission to review his audio clips to improve the technology. Experts like Philipp Koehn of Johns Hopkins and Lera Boroditsky of UC San Diego acknowledge that while machine translation is far from perfect, it enables connections previously impossible. The appâ€™s limitationsâ€”accent recognition, tone, pauses, and contextâ€”remain significant hurdles. Mr. Ferguson said in the letter that the â€œF.T.C. is not the speech policeâ€ but that consumers expected Apple News to offer neutral coverage.     [Original] ä¸­å›½åˆ›æ–°è¯å¯¹å¤–æˆæƒå¹´äº¤æ˜“é¢çªç ´åƒäº¿ç¾å…ƒï¼Œ4å¹´å¢é•¿è¿‘10å€
    New drug out-licensing deals involving Chinese biopharmaceutical companies reached a record high in 2025, surpassing the $100 billion mark. According to the latest data from data provider Pharmcube, Chinese companies signed out-licensing agreements worth a total of $137.7 billion in 2025, nearly a tenfold increase from 2021, with 186 transactions concluded. Global pharmaceutical giants including Novartis, AstraZeneca, and GSK signed multiple major agreements with Chinese firms last year. Tom Barsha, head of M&A for Bank of America Securities in the Asia-Pacific region, predicted that the total value of these licensing deals could double again within the next 18 to 24 months. "Global pharmaceutical companies are closely focusing on identifying next-generation innovative drug development pipelines in China and are evaluating various transaction structures," Barsha said.

    [Original] 2æœˆ14æ—¥ï¼šâ€œå†œäº§å“æ‰¹å‘ä»·æ ¼200æŒ‡æ•°â€æ¯”æ˜¨å¤©ä¸‹é™0.03ä¸ªç‚¹
    On February 14, data from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Affairs showed that the national agricultural product wholesale price index stood at 129.56, declining by 0.03 points from the previous day; the wholesale price index for "vegetable basket" products was 132.40, down 0.04 points. The average price of pork was 18.18 yuan per kilogram, a 0.2% decrease compared to the previous week; beef was 66.15 yuan per kilogram, down 0.7%; mutton was 65.58 yuan per kilogram, up 0.9%; eggs were 8.12 yuan per kilogram, down 2.3%; and fresh chicken was 17.29 yuan per kilogram, down 0.7%. Among the 28 key monitored vegetables, the average price was 5.58 yuan per kilogram, unchanged from the previous day; the average price of six key monitored fruits was 7.98 yuan per kilogram, down 1.0%. Regarding aquatic products, crucian carp was 20.00 yuan per kilogram, up 2.2%; common carp was 14.75 yuan per kilogram, up 1.9%; white carp was 10.56 yuan per kilogram, unchanged; and large yellow croaker was 44.58 yuan per kilogram, down 0.6%. Among the 46 key monitored varieties, the top five price increases were green pepper (+2.2%), crucian carp (+2.2%), Chinese cabbage (+2.1%), common carp (+1.9%), and pumpkin (+1.8%); the top five price decreases were white button mushroom (-3.3%), flower carp (-3.0%), eggs (-2.3%), Kyoho grape (-2.2%), and carrot (-1.9%). Overall, most agricultural product prices remained stable, with some aquatic products and vegetables seeing slight price increases, while prices for certain edible fungi and root vegetables declined.

    [Original] Head of Dubai-based ports giant quits after Epstein links revealed

While no wrongdoing is alleged, the emails show a close, wide-ranging relationship, including exchanges on travel plans, business ideas, and personal matters. The correspondence includes discussions of women, with Sulayem disparaging a â€œMoldavianâ€ woman in 2013 and later arranging for Epsteinâ€™s â€œprivate masseuseâ€ to be trained in Turkey.     [Original] Andrew facing claim he shared Treasury document with banking contact
    Prince Andrew Mountbatten-Windsor faces renewed scrutiny over allegations of misusing his public role, following the publication of emails revealing he shared a confidential Treasury briefing with Jonathan Rowland, a personal business associate. The 2010 emails, obtained by the Telegraph and verified by the Cabinet Office as authentic, show Andrew requested an update on the UK-Iceland deposit dispute, specifically regarding the deposit guarantee scheme. Shortly after receiving the document, he forwarded it to Rowland, asking for â€œcomment and a suggestion or solution,â€ noting that UK officials were urging caution before acting. Rowlandâ€™s father, David Rowland, had taken over part of Kaupthing, the largest Icelandic bank, which later became Banque Havilland. Jonathan Rowland, who served as CEO of Banque Havilland until 2013, told the BBC he had â€œno ideaâ€ about the reference in the emails and denied any contact with Jeffrey Epstein, though the Epstein files indicate Andrew referred to David Rowland as his â€œtrusted money manâ€ and promoted Banque Havilland to Epstein in October 2010. Epstein responded, â€œHis bank just might be the placeâ€¦ I guess I should learn more.â€ The files also suggest Banque Havilland made loans to Andrewâ€™s ex-wife, Sarah Ferguson, who faced financial difficulties. Banque Havilland lost its banking licence in 2024 and is appealing the decision. Rowland and his son deny any quid pro quo involving access to contacts, though they did not deny financial ties. Andrew Mountbatten-Windsor has denied any wrongdoing in his association with Epstein and has been contacted for comment. The Cabinet Office confirmed it is not disputing the emailsâ€™ authenticity and referred to Thames Valley Policeâ€™s ongoing assessment of whether to investigate possible misconduct in public office. The Times reported police had held informal discussions with government officials about the Epstein files and Andrewâ€™s conduct, though government sources said they were unaware of such talks but would not be surprised. The former prince served as the UKâ€™s trade envoy during the period in question.

    [Original] Heathrow not crowded but people walk in 'wrong place', says boss
    ShareSaveMitchell LabiakBusiness reporterShareSaveGetty ImagesHeathrow Airport's Terminal 5 is not crowded â€” people are just walking in the "wrong place", the airport's boss has said. Thomas Woldbye told an industry event "all the British people keep to the left and all the Europeans keep to the right", making the terminal feel crowded "when it's not actually". "And they do that in both directions, so we get everybody crashing into each other, and I see that from personal experience," he added. Heathrow is the UK's busiest airport, but its plans to build third runway have faced push-back from climate campaigners and locals despite government support. Woldbye told the Aviation Club UK event that, even though the government backed the expansion, he was "not sure of anything". "We have a very solid description of how that looks and what we're going to build. "What we don't have is necessary modernisation of airspace. "We don't have a long-term regulation which is clear in terms of building a business case," he said. He added that "lots of stuff has to be done this year in order to enable the actual commencement of building". Some 84 million passengers a year fly from Heathrow, but the airport says it could increase this to 150 million with a third runway. The government has said the expansion is badly needed to help economic growth, though some economists dispute this. Others are opposed to the expansion on environmental grounds and on the disruption it would cause to people who currently live near the airport. While the expansion may be a long way off, Woldbye told Aviation Club UK there were still "soft skills" the airport could use to manage more passengers â€” such stopping Europeans and Brits from bumping into each other. "We can change that," he said, adding the airport needs to make sure people going one way keep to a different side to people going the other direction. "And I know that's simplified, but that's the sort of thinking that you need." "We measure crowding, but we also measure people's perceptions of crowding... And interestingly, Terminal 3 has the best score and Terminal 5 has one of the worst, and there's way more space in Terminal 5, so what are we doing wrong?" He said the airport has removed some seating, telephone boxes, and other "clutter" in Terminal 3 and that it feels less crowded as a result, even though there are more people. "People feel more at ease... because they can see where they are going," he added.

    [Original] Amazon's Ring ends deal with surveillance firm after backlash
    Amazonâ€™s smart doorbell company, Ring, has canceled its planned partnership with Flock Safety, a surveillance technology firm, following intense public backlash over privacy concerns. The deal, announced in October, would have allowed law enforcement agencies using Flockâ€™s network of cameras and license plate readers to access video from Ring devices, provided customers had consented. However, Ring stated the integration â€œnever launched,â€ meaning no customer footage was ever shared with Flock. The company cited â€œsignificantly more time and resources than anticipatedâ€ as a key reason for the decision, while Flock described the cancellation as a â€œmutual decisionâ€ that allows both firms to better serve their customers and communities. The move follows widespread criticism of a Super Bowl ad for Ringâ€™s new â€œSearch Partyâ€ feature, which depicted neighbors using the tool to locate a lost dog. Critics labeled the ad â€œcreepy,â€ accusing it of normalizing mass surveillance. Senator Ed Markey (D-Mass.) called on Amazon to discontinue the feature, warning of a â€œcreepy surveillance state,â€ while the Electronic Frontier Foundation criticized the ad for masking a technology that could enable biometric tracking of people and pets. The ad drew mockery online, including a satirical response from rival company Wyze, whose video parody has been viewed nearly 100,000 times. Flock Safety, founded in 2017, operates in over 5,000 U.S. cities and primarily serves law enforcement agencies. Its partnership with Ring intensified scrutiny, especially amid heightened immigration enforcement under former President Donald Trump and concerns over misuse of surveillance data. Senator Ron Wyden (D-Ore.) had previously accused Flock of insufficient safeguards, noting potential abuse in targeting immigrants and women under abortion-related laws. Ring, acquired by Amazon in 2018, has faced ongoing privacy criticism and routinely receives thousands of law enforcement requests annually for customer footage, complying when legally required. Despite the cancellation, both companies continue to operate under public scrutiny regarding their roles in surveillance and data privacy.

    [Original] Inflation eases in US as prices for used cars fall
    Inflation in the United States slowed to a 2.4% year-on-year increase in January, down from 2.7% in December and the lowest rate since May, according to the Department of Labor. The consumer price index (CPI) decline was driven by falling energy prices, which dropped 1.5%, and a 1.8% decrease in used car and truck prices. Rents rose 0.2% from December, cooling from a 0.4% increase the prior month, while grocery staples saw moderated inflationâ€”steak prices fell over 2% from December, though they remain nearly 13% higher than a year agoâ€”and egg prices dropped more than 34% from January 2025. Despite the overall cooling, prices for personal services such as dry cleaning and haircuts rose 1.6% from December to January and were up nearly 7% year-on-year. Other notable price increases included cigarettes, airfares, and music streaming subscriptions. Analysts noted that while commodity prices excluding food and energy remained stable, the Federal Reserve still faces challenges in reaching its 2% inflation target, which it has missed for 59 consecutive months. The White House hailed the report as evidence of economic strength, with President Donald Trump declaring the U.S. economy â€œunbelievableâ€ and claiming he had â€œdefeated Joe Bidenâ€™s inflation crisis.â€ The administration urged the Federal Reserve to make â€œlong-overdueâ€ interest rate cuts, arguing that the economy is poised for further growth. Markets, however, reacted with muted enthusiasm, with current expectations pointing to a potential rate cut in June. Economists remain cautious. Atakan Bakiskan of Berenberg warned that persistent labor shortages could eventually drive wage growth and push up services inflation, potentially stalling progress toward the Fedâ€™s target. Neil Birrell, chief investment officer at Premier Miton Investors, said the January data â€œeases the path towards a cut in rates sooner rather than later,â€ citing strong growth, a firm job market, and stable inflation. Recent job growth also exceeded expectations, reinforcing the view that the economy is in solid shape. Still, analysts caution that the path to 2% inflation remains uncertain, particularly if tariffs lead to broader price increases or if service inflation remains sticky.

    [Original] Software? No Way. Weâ€™re an A.I. Company Now!
    When ChatGPT launched in November 2022, Intercom co-founder and CEO Eoghan McCabe faced an existential threat: if AI chatbots could handle customer service, demand for software like his would vanish. Within months, Intercom pivoted to an AI-first model, launching an AI customer service agent that helped drive annual recurring revenue to nearly $100 million. This transformation reflects a broader industry panic. Over the past year, software stocks have plummetedâ€”$2 trillion in market cap erased, with Salesforce and ServiceNow down over 40%â€”as investors and companies scramble to reposition as AI companies.     [Original] T.S.A. Workers Brace for Another Shutdown They Didnâ€™t Cause
    When the Department of Homeland Security ran out of funding early Saturday, Transportation Security Administration (T.S.A.) employees once again found themselves at the front lines of a congressional impasse, working without pay amid a government shutdown triggered by disagreements over the Trump administrationâ€™s immigration enforcement policies. With lawmakers departing without a funding agreement, T.S.A. staffâ€”already reeling from last yearâ€™s 43-day shutdownâ€”face renewed financial strain. Many employees, earning between $36,480 and $49,920 annually depending on location, are struggling with basic living costs, including rent, gas, medicine, and childcare. Some were evicted or could not afford transportation during the prior shutdown, and many remain angry they did not receive a promised $10,000 bonus for â€œexemplary serviceâ€ during that period, a reward never clearly defined and reportedly awarded unfairly. Roberto Echeverria, a lead transportation security officer at Salt Lake City International Airport and union member, said colleagues had been preparing for this scenario for weeks, accruing overtime for financial cushion. â€œHow many more times am I going to be able to do this?â€ he asked. Salt Lake City has lost nearly 100 officers since the last shutdown. Rebecca Wolf, president of the American Federation of Government Employees T.S.A. Local 1127, criticized the situation, noting that while T.S.A. officers work without pay, immigration enforcement personnel continue to be paid through a separate fund. â€œThis totally affects the wrong people,â€ she said. The latest shutdown follows a brief partial shutdown earlier this year and comes as the Trump administration seeks to eliminate T.S.A.â€™s collective bargaining rightsâ€”a move halted by a judge but still looming. Union leaders fear the threat undermines morale. Ha Nguyen McNeill, the T.S.A.â€™s senior official performing the administratorâ€™s duties, warned Congress that financial hardships could lead to last-minute absences, causing longer checkpoint lines, missed flights, and broader economic ripple effects. Travelers, already anxious over recent disruptions like the El Paso flight suspension, may face further delays. No word has been given on bonuses for this shutdown, despite past promises of rewards for â€œextraordinary efforts,â€ including working extra shifts. William Kincaid, a lead officer in Helena, Montana, said the lack of clear rules made the process feel like a game with no rules. Employees report minimal guidance from management, including orders to avoid social media while in uniform and not wearing T.S.A. jackets in public after an incident in Los Angeles where officers were mistaken for ICE agents. â€œWeâ€™re just helping people get through the airport so they can go on a trip,â€ Kincaid said. The uncertainty, combined with recurring pay issues and political fallout, continues to weigh heavily on T.S.A. personnel.

    [Original] Sick Detainees Describe Poor Care at CoreCivic ICE Facilities
    Measles outbreaks at two CoreCivic-operated immigration detention centers in Arizona and Texasâ€”separated by nearly 1,000 milesâ€”highlight systemic failures in medical care at facilities managed by the for-profit company. The outbreaks, which occurred last month, underscore broader issues including unsanitary conditions, delayed treatment, and inadequate staffing. Detainees and lawyers reported hours-long waits to see medical staff, only to be denied care unless symptoms were severe. Diabetes patients lacked consistent insulin access; those needing specialists like oncologists or dentists were frequently denied referrals. Children with stomach ailments were refused treatment unless they had vomited eight times. An 18-month-old at the Dilley center was hospitalized with dangerously low blood oxygen after weeks of unaddressed illness; a 35-year-old woman was initially denied care during a hemorrhage; and a 32-year-old man died at the Florence center after being detained despite severe diabetes and recent hospitalization for high blood sugar. CoreCivic, which operates 23% of ICEâ€™s detention facilities and is ICEâ€™s largest customer, disputes allegations, stating it prioritizes health and safety and routinely passes inspections. A company spokesperson, Steven Owen, claimed all detainees can access care, including emergencies, and that outside specialists are coordinated. However, federal audits and whistleblower accounts reveal a pattern of under-staffing, falsified records, and mismanagement. In 2022, the DHS inspector general found â€œcritical staffing shortagesâ€ at a CoreCivic facility in Torrance, NM, recommending immediate detainee removalâ€”never implemented. Whistleblowers alleged the company misrepresented compliance with safety standards. A San Diego nurse sued CoreCivic in 2024, alleging retaliation after reporting dangerous understaffingâ€”sometimes just two nurses for 1,500 detaineesâ€”leading to severe health complications. The case was settled confidentially. The Trump administrationâ€™s immigration crackdown has driven the detainee population to 68,000â€”up from 40,000 a year priorâ€”increasing demand for care among those with chronic illnesses, pregnant women, and elderly individuals. The Florence Immigrant and Refugee Rights Project noted a rise in detainees with serious medical conditions, including cancer. The death of 32-year-old Lorenzo Antonio Batrez Vargas, who had diabetes, a foot wound, and contracted Covid, has drawn scrutiny. His family described his death as a tragedy due to lack of medical attention. ICE confirmed he received care, but the cause remains under investigation. CoreCivic referred inquiries to ICE, maintaining that emergency care is always available. Despite past outbreaksâ€”including 31 measles cases in Eloy, Ariz., in 2016â€”CoreCivic continues to expand, including a new facility near Bakersfield, Calif., which began accepting detainees last summer.

    [Original] The 2026 Milan Olympics Has Its Eyes on Grana Padano
    Grana Padano, the 12th-century hard cheese produced in northern Italy, is making a prominent global appearance at the 2026 Winter Olympics in Milan and Cortina dâ€™Ampezzo, where it is featured on billboards, social media ads, and in athlete-friendly products like high-protein muffins and Olympic-branded snack bars. The cheese, which accounts for over 40% of hard cheese sales in Italian retail, is being promoted as a healthy, high-protein ally for athletes. The consortium overseeing its production is investing approximately $6.5 million in the Games, including widespread free distribution at venues. Mirella Parmeggiani, the consortiumâ€™s marketing and communications manager, stated the goal is to position Grana Padano as â€œan ally in the healthy diet of sports enthusiasts.â€ The return of the Olympics to Italy after 20 years offers a strategic platform to boost Italian food exports, which reached a record $70 billion in 2025, driven by brands like Prosecco and Gorgonzola. Italyâ€™s protected designation of origin (PDO) system ensures strict production standardsâ€”Grana Padano must be made from milk sourced in five northern regions and aged at least nine months. While Parmigiano-Reggiano, the more prestigious and expensive counterpart, has previously sponsored athletes like Giorgia Villaâ€”whose viral cheese-wheel gymnastics photos resurfaced after her 2024 Paris silver medalâ€”Grana Padano is now stepping into the spotlight. Unlike Parmigiano-Reggiano, which has partnered with the New York Jets and tennis tournaments, Grana Padano is focusing on Olympic visibility. Some regional producers, particularly in the Valtellina valley where Bormio and Livigno host skiing events, initially feared their local cheeses like Bitto and Valtellina Casera would be overshadowed. However, they were relieved to find Grana Padano did not restrict their marketing; visitors can now sample both mass-produced Grana Padanoâ€”nearly six million wheels annuallyâ€”and rare, artisanal Storico Ribelle, produced by just 12 cheesemakers. While concerns remain about the dominance of large cheese brands potentially eclipsing regional diversity, food journalist Eugenio Signoroni noted that the international visibility of big cheeses like Grana Padano ultimately benefits all of Italyâ€™s culinary heritage.

    [Original] Police activity under way near Nancy Guthrie's home
    ShareSaveAlexander Ledermanin Tucson, ArizonaShareSaveReutersPolice activity connected to the search for Nancy Guthrie, the missing mother of US news anchor Savannah Guthrie, is under way at a residence about two miles from her home. Armed police teams have been seen coming in and out the area, with a sheriff's vehicle blocking the road. It comes after local officials said investigators had found DNA at Guthrie's address which did not belong to her or anyone close to her. The 84-year-old disappeared in the middle of night from her home in Tucson, Arizona, nearly two weeks ago. Authorities believe she was taken against her will. The sheriff's department said in a social media post that "law enforcement activity" was ongoing "related to the Guthrie case" without providing further details. Pima County Sheriff Chris Nanos told local news station KOLD that investigators were "actively working a lead", the BBC's US news partner CBS reported. More than a dozen law enforcement vehicles, both marked and unmarked, have been seen in the area by BBC News, including Swat teams and forensics. Investigators have also found several gloves, with the closest discovered about two miles from Nancy Guthrie's home. The sheriff's department said reports that a glove was found inside her home or on the property were inaccurate. All collected evidence had been sent for laboratory analysis, they added. On Thursday, the FBI released a physical description of the suspect, describing them as a male between 5ft 9in and 5ft 10in (175-177cm) with an average build. It said investigators had been able to establish identifying details about the suspect after analysing footage from a doorbell camera outside Guthrie's home. The suspect was wearing a 25-litre Ozark Trail Hiker Pack backpack in the footage, the FBI said. After the doorbell footage was released, investigators received more than 13,000 tips, including 4,000 in the 24 hours. The FBI has also increased the reward for information about Guthrie's disappearance from $50,000 (Â£36,700) to $100,000. The county sheriff department said the suspect description "remains a key focus", but added that "investigators are not ruling out any individuals or possibilities". Investigators have also issued a wider appeal for video footage from Guthrie's neighbours. Police have said Nancy Guthrie, 84, needed daily medication and had limited mobility. Savannah Guthrie and her two siblings have released a number of social media pleas directed at their mother's abductor. They believe she is still alive and have indicated they would be willing to pay for her safe return.

    [Original] Casey Wasserman to sell talent agency after Epstein fallout
    ShareSaveRachel Muller-HeyndykShareSaveReutersProminent American agent Casey Wasserman is reportedly set to sell his talent company after documents linking him to Jeffrey Epstein and Ghislaine Maxwell were published in the US. Several high profile clients, including singer Chappell Roan, quit the firm this week after it emerged he flew on Epstein's private plane and exchanged flirtatious emails with Maxwell in 2003. US media reported Wasserman told employees he had "become a distraction" as he announced his intention to sell the major LA-based agency. The 51-year-old, who has also resisted calls to stand down from his role as chair of the 2028 Los Angeles Olympics, previously said he had no "personal or business relationship" with Epstein. "I'm deeply sorry that my past personal mistakes have caused you so much discomfort," Wasserman wrote in a memo on Friday, the Wall Street Journal reported. He continued: "It's not fair to you, and it's not fair to the clients and partners we represent so vigorously and care so deeply about." Wasserman has said he "deeply regrets" his discussions with Maxwell, who is serving a 20-year prison sentence for facilitating the sexual abuse of teenage girls by Epstein. He said his emails with Maxwell "took place over two decades ago, long before her horrific crimes came to light". Wasserman has not been accused of wrongdoing by any of Epstein's victims, and the appearance of his name in the files does not imply criminal activity of any kind. Earlier this week, LA28 said Wasserman would remain chairman of the 2028 games after organisers reviewed his past interactions with Maxwell. They found his relationship did not go further than the exchanges that had already been documented, and that he had fully cooperated with an investigation. In a statement, the LA28 board said Wasserman and his then-wife flew on a humanitarian mission to Africa on Epstein's plane at the invitation of the Clinton Foundation in 2003. The board said the journey was long before "Wasserman or the public knew of Epstein and Maxwell's deplorable crimes". "This was his single interaction with Epstein. Shortly after, he traded the publicly-known emails with Maxwell," the statement continued. A number of stars have have walked away from Wasserman's agency in recent days. In an Instagram post on Tuesday, singer Chappell Roan announced that she would no longer be working with Wasserman. She said: "No artist, agent or employee should ever be expected to defend or overlook actions that conflict so deeply with our own moral values." Roan did not specifically mention the Epstein-related documents in her statement. Former US footballer player Abby Wambach also said she was leaving the agency, saying: "I know what I know and I am following my gut and values. I will not participate in any business arrangement under his leadership."

    [Original] Six possible effects of Trump's climate policy change
    US President Donald Trump has reversed the 2009 EPA endangerment finding, a cornerstone of Obama-era environmental policy that classified six greenhouse gasesâ€”including carbon dioxide and methaneâ€”as threats to public health and the environment. The decision, announced by the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), dismantles the legal foundation for regulating emissions under the Clean Air Act, paving the way for looser rules on industries, particularly automakers. The EPA stated that maintaining emissions standards is not essential to its "core mission," despite scientific consensus that greenhouse gases contribute to health issues and premature deaths. The Environmental Defense Fund projects that, without the finding, the US could emit 7.5 to 18 billion additional tonnes of greenhouse gases by 2055â€”three times current annual emissionsâ€”potentially causing 15,400 to 58,000 premature deaths, tens of millions of additional asthma attacks, and tens of thousands more hospital visits. The White House claims the move will save automakers $2,400 per vehicle and taxpayers over $1.3 trillion, calling it "the single largest deregulatory action in US history." Industry groups like Ford and the Alliance for Automotive Innovation welcomed the rollback, citing unachievable standards under previous administrations. However, experts warn the reversal undermines global climate leadership. Former EPA head Margo Oge and former Secretary of State John Kerry criticized the move, noting that while the US retreats from clean vehicle standards, China and the EU are expanding renewable energy and electric vehicle markets. Kerry warned the policy will "cost lives" and exacerbate climate-driven disasters. Legal experts also predict a surge in public nuisance lawsuits, as the 2011 Supreme Court ruling that granted the EPA exclusive authority over emissions regulation is now at risk. Without the endangerment finding, states and communities may again sue polluters directly. Robert Percival of the University of Maryland cautioned that the administrationâ€™s overreach could backfire. Critics argue that shifting manufacturing to countries like China and Indiaâ€”where production is often dirtierâ€”does not reduce global emissions. Diana Furchtgott-Roth, a former DOT official, echoed this, stating that offshoring emissions does not lower global totals. The decision has sparked legal challenges from environmental groups and raises concerns about the US falling behind in the global clean energy race.

    [Original] Chinaâ€™s gold rush: why families are doubling down on precious metals
    Gold is becoming more popular in China ahead of the Lunar New Year, with households viewing the asset as a safety net amid an uncertain economy People across China are buying up gold in large volumes ahead of the Lunar New Year holiday, as surging prices for the precious metal fuel its popularity as both a festive gift and an investment. From migrant workers splashing out on gold-coated jewellery, to white-collar workers pouring their savings into gold-linked investment funds, the metal is widely seen not only as a marker of social respectability, but also as a safety net amid an uncertain world. The price spike has sparked a surge in sales of gold-plated silver jewellery in Chinese factory hubs such as Dongguan. Gift-giving is a huge part of the Lunar New Year, as millions of migrant workers return to their hometowns laden with boxes of food, cash-filled red envelopes and other presents for their relatives and prospective partners. And with prices for both gold and silver soaring, gold-plated jewellery is becoming a popular gift: it is more affordable than pure gold items, but is still likely to hold its value, explained Chen Li, a sales assistant at a jewellery shop in Dongguan. â€œInquiries and sales of gold-plated silver items have noticeably increased ahead of the Lunar New Year, mainly from migrant workers at nearby factories,â€ Chen said, adding that the recent spike in silver prices was likely to fuel the trend even more this year.

    [Original] å¥³å­ä¹°6å…ƒå½©ç¥¨ä¸­1204ä¸‡
    A 30-something female lottery player from Nanjing, Jiangsu Province, purchased a 6-yuan randomly generated Double Color Ball ticket at a lottery outlet in Gulou District on October 15. After the draw that evening, her ticket matched all the winning numbers exactly, winning her the top prize of 12.04 million yuanâ€”the highest single-ticket jackpot ever recorded in Nanjing for the Double Color Ball game and also the largest lottery prize in Jiangsu Province in recent times. According to the Jiangsu Welfare Lottery Issuance Center, the winner is an ordinary citizen whose identity has not been disclosed and is referred to only as a "Nanjing lottery player." She stated that she has a stable job with average income, and that playing the lottery is merely an occasional pastime, never expecting to win. At the prize claim site, she expressed emotional excitement, saying she plans to use the winnings to improve her family's living conditions, including purchasing property for her parents, while retaining part of the funds for investment and financial management to achieve steady wealth growth. The odds of winning the Double Color Ball jackpot are approximately one in 17.72 million, and this win once again highlights the randomness and unpredictability of lottery draws. Industry experts pointed out that lottery public welfare funds continue to support key social sectors such as education, healthcare, and elderly care. This major prize not only transforms an individual's life but also strengthens public awareness of the social welfare nature of lotteries. Experts caution that lottery playing should be approached rationally, avoiding addiction, and that winning should never be regarded as a primary life expectation. Lottery agencies across multiple regions are using this opportunity to intensify public awareness campaigns, promoting the principle of "play within one's means and gamble responsibly." The prize disbursement process has now been completed, and the winner said she will handle follow-up matters discreetly, hoping to return to a peaceful, ordinary life.

    [Original] ç‹æ¯…ï¼šä¸­å›½äººä¸æ¥å—é«˜å¸‚æ¶‰å°é”™è¯¯è¨€è®º
    Chinese Foreign Minister Wang Yi recently stated a firm position on the Taiwan issue during an international conference, clearly emphasizing that "the Chinese people do not accept inappropriate remarks about Taiwan made under the name of 'Gaoshi'." In response to recent improper statements on Taiwan made under the name of "Gaoshi" (referring to Kaohsiung City, Taiwan region) at certain international forums, Beijing expressed strong dissatisfaction. Wang Yi stressed that Taiwan is an inseparable part of China, and any remarks challenging the one-China principle are unacceptable. In recent years, some countries and organizations have repeatedly tested China's red lines on the Taiwan issue, attempting to undermine the international consensus on the one-China principle through measures such as supporting so-called "local representatives" to participate in international activities and promoting the internationalization of "Taiwan independence" forces. The recent "Gaoshi" remarks were viewed by China as another example of such behavior. Wang Yi pointed out that such statements violate the universally recognized one-China principle, seriously undermine China's sovereignty and territorial integrity, and disrupt regional peace and stability. China reiterated that the Taiwan issue must not be subject to external interference, and any attempt to create a "two Chinas" or "one China, one Taiwan" under the guise of "local" representation will be firmly opposed by the Chinese government and people. Wang Yi called on relevant countries and international organizations to abide by the one-China principle, respect China's core interests, and refrain from providing platforms or space for "Taiwan independence" separatist forces. Analysts believe this statement is not only a response to a specific incident but also a significant manifestation of China's continuous reinforcement of its sovereignty discourse and defense of national core interests in a complex international environment. In the future, China may adopt more diplomatic and public opinion measures to further consolidate international consensus on the one-China principle and curb the international space available to "Taiwan independence" separatist activities.
